# Algorithmic Trading and Finance Models with Python, R, and Stata Essential Training

> Many stock market trades are conducted with algorithms, or “algos,” computer programs that buy or sell stocks according to mathematical formulas. These equity trades happen at a speed and frequency that humans cannot replicate. It's important for finance professionals and everyone who invests in the stock market to understand how these algorithms work. In this course, Professor Michael McDonald sh

### 1. The Basics of Algo Trading

#### Basics of algo trading
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] It's important to understand when we're talking about the financial industry, the industry's evolving.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=5)** The reality is, whether we like it or not, computers are playing a bigger and bigger role.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=9)** Algorithmic or computer-driven trading now makes up the large majority of trades in the financial markets.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=16)** More than 90% of orders are algorithm by some metrics and estimates.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=23)** So you might wonder, "Where do humans come in?"
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=25)** Well, the reality is humans still play a role in trading.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=29)** Among other things, humans design algorithms.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=32)** Computers are great at executing the trades, carrying out the strategy that humans have developed.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=39)** So the role that you should think of for yourself from an algorithmic trading perspective is you are the general that tells all your computer soldiers what to do.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=49)** That means that you need to be familiar with how the markets work and how to develop those algorithmic trading strategies.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=56)** That's what this course is all about.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=58)** Now, how does algorithmic trading work?
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=60)** Well, essentially, all algorithmic trading relies on kind of a four-step process.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=65)** We're going to start with some sort of pre-trade analysis.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=69)** This is built around coming up with the strategy that we're going to follow in our algorithmic trading.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=75)** What is the model that we are using to try and generate positive returns?
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=81)** This could be based on technical factors, it could be based on fundamental research, but whatever we're doing, we need some sort of a quantitative model that a computer can then use to identify attractive trading opportunities.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=95)** This is where the trading signal comes into play.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=98)** Once we've figured out what our strategy is, the computer then will evaluate our strategy and look for opportunities in the markets.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=108)** Here's a dumb example.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=109)** Let's pretend that we think that stocks that begin with M will go up on Mondays, and stocks that begin with T will go up on Tuesdays.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=117)** Well, the computer would go through and find all the stocks that begin with M on Mondays and say that we should buy those.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=124)** The pre-trade analysis is figuring out what letter stock we should buy.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=129)** The trading signal then goes through and identifies those stocks.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=132)** Then we execute that trade.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=135)** The trade gets pushed through.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=136)** We do any sort of post-trade analysis to make sure that the model's working is appropriate, and we start the whole process over again.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=144)** This relies on two key inputs: Data and research to help us understand that data.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=151)** These factors are critical in putting together an effective algorithmic trading strategy.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=157)** Now, algorithmic trading, or algo trading for short, essentially comes in two flavors: Market making and data mining.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=164)** Market making trades are attempting to capitalize on what's called the bid-ask spread.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=168)** That is the difference between what people will buy or sell a stock for.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=171)** This is typically associated with high-frequency traders.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=175)** Data mining, instead, is based on patterns in data, things like stock prices and then outside information.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=182)** Essentially, here, we're looking for correlations or relationships between stock prices and other data points, and then trying to capitalize on it.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/basics-of-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=191)** And at a high level, that's what algorithmic trading is all about.

#### Market making with algos
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the two major types of algorithmic trading is what's called market making.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=4)** Market making, as the name implies, is all about making an effective market, it's about helping to match up buyers and sellers.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=12)** Computers are really good at this type of repetitive minutiae that helps to markets to function more efficiently.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=20)** Now, as part of the market, we have two specific types of orders that comes in, offers and bids, often called bid and ask.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=31)** Essentially, bids just represent individuals who are willing to come in and bid or buy a stock and they put in an order at a specific price.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=41)** So in this particular example, we have a stock trading for around $113.10.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=47)** We have one party willing to buy 600 shares at $113.10.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=54)** Another party willing to pay to buy 725 shares at $113.9, and then another party willing to buy 150 shares at $113.8.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=65)** We have this bid side of the book built up, higher prices go to the top of the book.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=70)** Those represent the best possible purchase orders.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=74)** On the other side of the coin, we have the asks or offers, these represent offers to sell.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=81)** In this particular case, again, just like the bid side, we have them stacked up over time.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=86)** So we have someone willing to sell 1,255 shares at 113.13.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=92)** We have someone willing to sell 480 shares at 113.12, someone willing to sell 825 shares at $113.11.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=102)** These bids and asks have to match against one another in order to make the market effectively.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=109)** In this case, our price is going to be $113.10 based on those bids and asks.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=117)** Now, there's a variety of different types of orders that'll come in over time to the market.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=122)** To begin with, we have market orders.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=125)** These are the simplest types of orders.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=127)** Essentially, an investor comes in and says they want to either buy or sell a stock at whatever the best available price is.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=133)** That order will then get executed immediately, just like that.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=138)** Second, we have limit orders.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=140)** Limit orders really represent haggling.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=142)** We have somebody who comes in and says, "Well, I want to buy 500 shares, but only if I can get it for $113.1."
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=151)** They have a specific price in mind.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=153)** And then finally, we have what are called iceberg orders.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=156)** These are large orders that get divided up into smaller lots so that they don't overwhelm the supply and demand in the market and push that price in the wrong direction for the order entrant.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=170)** In addition to the type of order, there are also specific terms and conditions around the order.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=175)** So one of those terms and conditions is the time and force.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=178)** Day orders are orders where they're valid for less than a day.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=182)** This order needs to get filled before the end of the day or it gets canceled.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=187)** We also have what called good till canceled orders.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=190)** These get executed immediately or else they get put in the order book and left there until the person that entered that order goes through and cancels it.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=200)** Good till canceled orders are valid if they get executed immediately, or alternatively, if they're not executed immediately, then they get left on the order book until they are either executed or canceled by the individual that put in the order, whom I'm calling the entrant.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=217)** Finally, we have fill or kill orders.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=220)** These are orders where they need to be either immediately executed or they get canceled.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=227)** In addition to the basic types of orders and the conditions, we also have what are called conditional orders.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=233)** So these are orders where they're going to be put in if a specific condition occurs.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=239)** A stop order, for example, says we're going to sell a specific security, specific stock, if that stock's price falls to a particular level.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=250)** Alternatively, we could offer to buy a specific stock if the price rises to a particular level.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=257)** The idea here is that we're putting in an order and then we let a computer handle the details.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=263)** We set what the limits are when that order should be executed or not, and then the computer waits until we have conditions that match our orders.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=272)** Similarly, we have what's called a stop limit order.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=275)** This is an order that gets executed at the exact price we specify or better.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=280)** It's very similar to the standard stop order.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=283)** It's just that we put in a limit order rather than a market order once those particular conditions are met.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=290)** And then finally, and this type of order would not be algorithmic, we have what are called discretionary orders.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=296)** This is when a traditional human broker decides when to place the order, what the price should be, et cetera.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=304)** Prior to the advent of algorithmic trading and prior to the rise of the internet, this was sort of the traditional order where you called up your broker, the broker would then put in the order on your behalf and try to do the best job for you.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/market-making-with-algos?u=76281980&t=317)** In essence, this is what algorithmic trading competes against.

#### Prop trading with algos
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=34)** You've got to have a codeable rule, determining when you're going to buy or sell.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=39)** Then we've got to go through and set operating time horizons and constraints.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=44)** This requires that we're going to pull in data and performance statistics that we can monitor over time.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=51)** Typically, humans are going to program these algorithms and then they're going to provide oversight to the algorithms, but the algorithms are the one actually executing all of the trades.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=62)** This means that we need programmable start and stop rules.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=66)** Moreover, we're also going to have to be very careful about tracking our results, meaning our profit and loss, any risk metrics we care about, et cetera, so that we can make sure the algorithm isn't out of control, if you will, meaning that the algorithm isn't taking more risk than we want it to, or the mark conditions haven't deteriorated, as a result, making our algorithm no longer valid.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=88)** And related to that, we're going to need to do testing on our algorithm, both backtesting before we start the algorithm and then continual testing over time to make sure that the algorithm's level of risk is staying within our confidence interval or our tolerance.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=105)** All of this falls into the category of kind of maintaining that algorithm.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=109)** Typically, algorithms are going to need continual monitoring and maintenance.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=114)** Once we've set up the algorithm though, you don't want to go and tinker with it.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=117)** You don't want to take something that's working and risk breaking it.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=121)** So instead, keep that algorithm that's working, monitor its performance, monitor the market conditions, be very careful not to let your oversight lapse, and then rejuvenate that algorithm as conditions warrant.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=135)** Algorithms all deteriorate or degenerate over time, trading strategies become outdated, other people figure them out, and as a result, the alpha that's generated by that trading strategy gets competed away.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=149)** So we may end up decommissioning the algorithm over time, but you want to make that decision with clear data in mind rather than doing that on an ad hoc basis.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=159)** Now, here's an example where we might look at an algorithm, right?
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=164)** So this graph shows us the intraday price of the euro versus the U.S. dollar.

>

>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=178)** What we see here is the number of quotes over time and then the trading day.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=183)** What we observe, unsurprisingly, is that kind of in the middle of the trading day when New York and London are open, we have the highest level of volume going on in this particular currency pair.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=198)** After New York and Europe close and before the Asian markets open, we have a lot less trading volume.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=203)** So if you wanted to try to build an algorithm around this, you might try to capitalize on demand that occurs as some of the markets open, say London and New York.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=214)** So we would try to capitalize on any kind of demand spike that we see in the middle of the day, and then sell towards the end of the day as demand is going to wane.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=224)** This is something we'll touch on later in the course.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=227)** Algorithmic trading does have specific requirements from a technical perspective.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=232)** So again, humans are critical to actually designing that algorithm, but beyond the human role, beyond the data and the strategy and all of that, you are going to need certain technical requirements in order to make this particular type of trading work.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=247)** In particular, you need a centralized order book.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=250)** So you have to have some sort of a shared, centralized book that lists the buy and sell orders for specific securities over a particular period of time.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=259)** This is how you're going to test whether or not you should be buying or selling.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=264)** Similarly, we need to have access to the markets, and they need to be highly liquid markets, ideally, with high frequency trading options available.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=273)** So this will be things like equities, futures, derivatives, bonds, FX, et cetera.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=278)** You're not going to be able to do algorithmic trading in real estate, as an example.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=282)** You're not going to be able to do algorithmic trading in a lot of the the foreign markets, where the volume simply isn't there.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=289)** The illiquidity will eat up all the alpha that your algorithm would generate.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=294)** Moreover, you're going to need to have three specific types of systems in order to support your algorithmic trading.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=301)** You're going to need to have in-house systems to enable your proprietary trading and market-making type decisions.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=307)** You'll need to have client systems that, as an example, the bank's clients might use, or that you as a client of the bank can use, depending on whether you work for the bank or you're an outside client.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=318)** And then you need to have vendor systems sold by third parties that help you with this algorithmic trading.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=324)** Finally, you're going to need some sort of an information exchange that'll help to deal with the financial protocols necessary to give you access to the exchange and allow you to make these buy and sell decisions.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/prop-trading-with-algos?u=76281980&t=338)** Put all of this together and you'll be on the road to a successful start in algorithmic trading.

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/textual-analysis-and-algo-trading?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/textual-analysis-and-algo-trading?u=76281980&t=8)** Text data, as the name implies, is something where it's not just numbers that are coming in, but instead, all kinds of qualitative information.

#### Careers in algorithmic trading
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now, one question that comes up all the time when people talk to me about algorithmic trading is, "Gee, I'm really interested in this space.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980&t=7)** How do I get a job in it?"
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980&t=9)** Well, algorithmic trading is a great role to begin.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980&t=12)** The field has grown dramatically, it tends to be lucrative, and the future looks bright, but you need to understand algorithmic trading as a career before you jump in.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980&t=24)** So first of all, what is it that algorithmic traders do?
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980&t=26)** Well, the reality is that in most cases that I've seen, and in my previous experience in the industry, typically a finance guy gets paired up with a computer programmer CS guy, and essentially the finance guy's role is to conceptualize possible strategies to come up with what's the theory that we're trying to capitalize on or trade on.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/careers-in-algorithmic-trading?u=76281980&t=50)** And then it's the programmer's role to turn around and create programmable tools that will evaluate those particular strategies.

#### Financial data and Python
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/financial-data-and-python?u=76281980)

>
> **[9:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/testing-strategies-in-stata?u=76281980&t=565)** What we've done here is show, through a basic back test, our triangular arbitrage strategy should be profitable.
>
> **[9:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/testing-strategies-in-stata?u=76281980&t=574)** Based on that, we've created a buy, no-buy decision.

>
> **[10:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/testing-strategies-in-stata?u=76281980&t=605)** From there, we'd feed that buy decision into our execution algorithm to tell it to ship this trade off to the exchange, or else don't do anything, and that's how we'd go through and build a real algorithmic trading system from soup to nuts.

### 5. Data and Trading

#### Getting broad market data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/getting-broad-market-data?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/getting-broad-market-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If you're going to do algorithmic trading, realistically you're going to need data.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/getting-broad-market-data?u=76281980&t=4)** Let's talk about some options for where you can get that data.

>

>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/getting-broad-market-data?u=76281980&t=24)** In other words, you need historical data so that you can come up with some sort of a strategy based on backtesting, and then you need real-time data to enable you to go through and use a rules-based asset management approach.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/getting-broad-market-data?u=76281980&t=37)** Now, there's many different sources of financial data that are out there.

>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/getting-broad-market-data?u=76281980&t=55)** So, FactSet is certainly something you should be thinking about as a starting point here.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/getting-broad-market-data?u=76281980&t=61)** But algorithmic trading is a little different than, say, wealth management, or running a hedge fund, or something like that, in that you need large amounts of data, you need copious amounts of data, and you need it in a machine-readable form, and so in that case, you really, most of the time, need different APIs.

#### Finding strategies in investing: Factors
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/finding-strategies-in-investing-factors?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/finding-strategies-in-investing-factors?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] When people think about algorithmic trading, they usually think about high-frequency trading, that is trading multiple times per day, or oftentimes multiple times per second or minute.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/finding-strategies-in-investing-factors?u=76281980&t=10)** It doesn't have to be that way.
>

#### Model aging and obsolescence
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/model-aging-and-obsolescence?u=76281980)

> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/model-aging-and-obsolescence?u=76281980&t=336)** And then, ideally, you have access to data or you have thought of something that somebody else hasn't thought of, and that will make that strategy more persistent and long-lasting over time.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/algorithmic-trading-and-finance-models-with-python-r-and-stata-essential-training-24504280/model-aging-and-obsolescence?u=76281980&t=349)** If it's not persistent and long-lasting over time, you are going to need to be prepared to modify your approach as the alpha deteriorates over time.
